2.2 when
He's legit gut making a game engine at this point.  Scripting- can be pulled off with triggers.  spawn trigger can act as function. some sort of if statement with count triggers, can only count interger values tho. prob only functional programming only, no oop. Variables can only be global interger values (but... almost anything can be represented as an interger value if you know what type the variable is)  Animation - move trigger and now a trigger KEYFRAME TRIGGER!  Collision - object and trigger  Graphics - you have a whole arsenal of stuff the skies the limit, jesus...  Gameplay - various speeds, jump pads, portals, sizes, game modes (ie. dual or platformer)   Save game- can be done with a key system, can't write something to disk tho.  Sound effects - eh not really. (Maybe could be done with a VERY polished system where a ng song has various sound effects, and when you do something the song trigger moves to that sound in the song, you would also probably have to make a bunch of spawn triggers detecting how long EACH SOUND IS so when that sound is done it then goes back to a silent part in the song so it doesn't keep playing other sounds)   Music - either or, sound or music. Cant play two songs at once in gd. Would work the same as the sound trigger, but with music and a sound looping system.  Editing to add some more...  Camera - trigger to control it.  Shaders - trigger, can do many screen effects now.  GUI - can be possible, but way harder without a simple mouse detecting trigger...

We've been wrong this whole time... The thing we call the "player" the thing we try to stop from death, the very thing we sought to protect was the villain all along. It's mission was not avoiding death, but instead it's mission was to die. An explosion nearly powerful enough to tear through the very fabric of space-time. Thousands of years ago RubRub was entrusted with millions of universes, each with its unique buildings and monuments.  However evil forces sought to destroy every last one and take their power orbs until the only universe remaining was their own that they rule over. RubRub used all the energy in millions of orbs to create one defensive building per universe... The great wall... capable of turning any weapon back into the orbs it was crafted from. The evil forces built up an army of cube shaped bombs they attacked all at oncefrom behind one cube per world. The cube army was attacking from the opposite side RubRub expected and the great wall lay miles away in the distance. RubRub hacked and gained control of the cubes but he knew he couldn't stop them all. So he recruited you agreeing to reward you with orbs from the cubes you disarm. The closer you get the cubes to the great wall the weaker they become and the .ore orbs you get. So next time you load up geometry dash remember your not playing as a gamer but as a protector of worlds.

In production since 1948, the F-Series is a range of light-duty trucks marketed as full-size pickup trucks, slotted above the compact Ford Ranger in the Ford truck model range. Since 1999, the F-Series also includes the heavier-duty Super Duty series, which includes pickup trucks, chassis cab trucks, and medium-duty trucks. As of current production, the Ford F-Series includes the F-150 pickup, F-250 through F-450 Super Duty pickups, F-450/550 Super Duty chassis cabs, and F-650/750 Super Duty Class 6-8 trucks. The most popular version of the F-Series is the F-150, now in its fourteenth generation.
